2.7 Independence, RNG attestations, ethics
Purpose. Guarantee that Nexus data are free of inter-member classical coordination, that all randomized choices are unpredictable and auditable, and that human subjects protections, privacy, and safety are upheld. Independence and RNG attestations are gates for Â§2.3â€“Â§2.6; ethics governs participation and data handling.

2.7.1 Independence audits (no classical side channels)
Physical isolation (site hygiene).
(i) RF: Faraday enclosure or certified RF-quiet room; continuous spectrum scan f âˆˆ [10 Hz, 6 GHz].
(ii) Network: air-gapped devices; no shared LAN, Bluetooth, Wi-Fi, or serial links.
(iii) Optical/acoustic: light baffles; acoustic damping; background mics for PSD veto.
(iv) Power: filtered, isolated supplies; line monitors to veto correlated spikes.
(v) Clocking: no shared low-latency clock lines; only LF timestamps with bounded skew Î´tâ‚clkâ‚.
Statistical independence tests (per window Î“).

Random, preregistered injects: RF tone bursts, optical flicker, power-line tickles, and dummy notifications near devices. Any detectable imprint in cross-member channels above thresholds voids independence for Î“.
Pass rule. All physical checks green, and all stats bounds satisfied with permutation-null q â‰¤ Î±â‚indâ‚. Failures disqualify Î“ from entanglement claims (Â§2.3) and ignition (Â§2.6).

2.7.2 RNG attestations (unpredictable, auditable settings)
Entropy sources and derivation.
(i) Public beacon B(t) (verifiable, append-only).
(ii) Local QRNG streams Eâ‚siteâ‚.
Derive per-shot seeds by KDF: sâ‚k,iâ‚ = cSHAKE256( B(tâ‚k,iâ‚) âˆ¥ Eâ‚siteâ‚ âˆ¥ meta ), producing axis choices a âˆˆ {x, y, z} and trial schedules.

Anti-precompute discipline.
Settings are derived after tâ‚k,iâ‚ âˆ’ Î´ with Î´ â‰¤ Î´tâ‚clkâ‚, enforced by a verifiable delay step or time-lock in the KDF pipeline. Any early derivation flags the shot.
Quality checks.

2.7.3 Ethics, privacy, and governance
Consent and scope.
Participants enroll under written consent describing tasks, randomization, data collected, risks, and withdrawal rights. No deception beyond randomization; debrief available on request.
Data minimization and pseudonymity.
Member identities are mapped to pseudonymous IDs; only {timestamps, axes, outcomes, device QC, environmental vetoes} are stored for analysis. No audio/video beyond environmental veto channels is retained.
Safety and workload.
Session length, rest breaks, and fatigue screens are preregistered. Participants may pause or withdraw at any time without penalty.
Privacy controls.
Per-window ops cards contain only pseudonymous metadata and cryptographic hashes. Sharing outside the core team uses aggregated statistics or differentially private summaries when individual-level release is required.
Governance.
An independent review board oversees protocol changes; any change creates a new versioned preregistration and cannot retroactively affect prior windows.

Rationale. These attestations close the principal loopholes: classical coordination, predictability of settings, and human-subjects risk. They are operational, auditable, and reproducible, and they keep the Nexus layer cleanly separable from Ï‡-transport claims downstream.

3.1 Variables and near-isotropic closure (u, F = câ‚Ï‡â‚ u nÌ‚)

4.1 Momentum deposition: fâ‚depâ‚ = (ÎºÏ/câ‚Ï‡â‚)Â·F
Statement (force density).

fâ‚depâ‚(t, x) â‰¡ (ÎºÂ·Ï(t, x)/câ‚Ï‡â‚)Â·F(t, x).

4.1.1 Where this comes from (conservation + symmetry)Momentum conservation (Ï‡ â†’ matter). The Ï‡ flux carries momentum density Pâ‚Ï‡â‚ = F/câ‚Ï‡â‚. Any local attenuation or redirection of F transfers momentum to matter. 6.3 Ignition transient kernel (Aâ‚shâ‚, Ï„â‚shâ‚)

7.2 Sunâ†”Earth Î³-foil test (monopole lag scan; Bayes factor)

8.3.2 Polarization content (no extra modes)
The Ï‡ closure (F = câ‚Ï‡â‚ u nÌ‚, â€–nÌ‚â€– = 1) adds no propagating scalar or vector degree of freedom to the metric sector. In TT gauge the radiative solution carries only the + and Ã— polarizations; any Ï‡-induced anisotropy affects the source stress at O(Îµ) but does not project into additional GW polarizations at O(Îµâ°). Preferred-frame and non-conservative PPN slots remain null (Â§8.2).

8.3.3 Speed and dispersion (guardrails)
Because the GW equation is â–¡â€‰\bar hâ‚Î¼Î½â‚ = source, there is no mass term, no frequency-dependent index, and thus no dispersion to leading order. Sector consistency demands câ‚gwâ‚ = 1; our Ï‡ propagation speed câ‚Ï‡â‚ â‰¤ 1 is a separate medium property and does not mix into the GW kinetic term.

8.3.4 Source-level effects vs propagationAstrophysical sources. If a GW source resides entirely outside any Ï‡-attenuating domain, its waveform is identical to GR. If a source sits inside a domain where Î¸â‚Gâ‚(tâ‚sourceâ‚) drifts adiabatically, the chirp-rate prefactor rescales through Î¼(t) = Gâ‚Nâ‚ Î¸â‚Gâ‚(t) M, but this is a source modeling choice, not a propagation change. Our lab program uses windows where external sources are effectively GR-standard.Lab domain. GWs traversing the lab are metric perturbations; they do not scatter on Ï‡ because the metric kinetic term is unchanged. The boundary dial ğ’œâ‚00â‚(t) does not couple to hâ‚Î¼Î½â‚.8.3.5 Detector response and calibration
Interferometer test masses and clocks respond to the metric tidal field as in GR. Composition independence holds (EP-safe push law fâ‚depâ‚ âˆ Ï acts on Newtonian forces, not on GW geodesic deviation). Any slow drift in Î¸â‚Gâ‚(t) affects local Newtonian calibrations (e.g., pendulum bias) but not the relativistic transfer function of a GW detector; we treat such biases as monitored systematics in the instrument model.

8.3.6 Energy flux and conservation
GW energy flux and backreaction follow standard GR formulas. Ï‡â€“matter exchange Qâ½Î½â¾ accounts for momentum deposition fâ‚depâ‚ in the Newtonian sector without adding attenuation to GWs. There is no Ï‡-induced damping of GWs and no extra radiative channel for hâ‚Î¼Î½â‚ at leading order.

8.3.7 Anisotropy and solar foil (irrelevance to GWs)
The low-rank anisotropy {Aâ‚1â‚, Aâ‚triâ‚} lives in the Ï‡ boundary intensity and appears only as a tiny nuisance in Newton-like forces (O(Îµâ½2â¾) on pair magnitudes; Â§4.4). It carries no TT power. The optional Sun-locked foil Î³ modifies only the monopole dial and cannot alter GW propagation or polarization (Â§7.2).

8.3.8 Contract (what to use in practice)Use standard GR GW templates (TT-only, câ‚gwâ‚ = 1).Treat any Ï‡ influence only through slow, source-side Î¸â‚Gâ‚(t) (if modeling such sources) or through independent Newtonian calibration channels in the lab.Do not introduce extra polarizations, dispersion, or birefringence from Ï‡.With these guardrails, the GW sector is unchanged at leading order, fully compatible with Â§8.2 and the boundary-first Ï‡ dynamics that govern Î¸â‚Gâ‚(t) in the Newtonian/PN analyses.

15.3 Guardrails: PPNâ„GW, EM-drift null, positivityâ„unitarity, subluminality, cosmology neutrality, composition null

16.1 Claim threshold and failure modes
Purpose. Fix the minimum evidence to assert a positive detection of boundary-driven gravity control and list fail-fast failure modes with prescribed quarantine paths. All rules are preregistered; no post-hoc tuning.

16.1.1 Decision rule (primary claim)
We claim a positive detection only if all of the following hold:Two-lab + LLR coherence.
At least two independent lab channels among {SCG, Tor, Clk} pass their tests and the LLR annual arc is consistent with the same post-step level Î¸Ì„ (sign and size within propagated errors).Four test batteries pass (Â§14.2), each with preregistered thresholds:

(ii) OU isotropization detected: log-ğ“‘â‚Aâ‚ â‰¥ ln 10 with a common Ï„Ì‚â‚Aâ‚ across lab channels.
(iii) Causal lags satisfied: vÌ‚â‚frontâ‚ â‰¤ 1, no pre-cone power, and câ‚Ï‡â‚ prior truncated to [vÌ‚â‚frontâ‚, 1].
(iv) Solar foil neutralized: log-ğ“‘â‚Î³â‰¡0:freeâ‚ â‰¥ ln 10 (favoring Î³ = 0).Predictive adequacy.

Independent re-analysis (audit team) reproduces Î¸â‚Gâ‚(t), vÌ‚â‚frontâ‚, Ï„Ì‚â‚Aâ‚ from the released packs within 1Ïƒ; SHA-256 roots match the ToE receipt.Outcome. If (1)â€“(5) hold, we mint a ToE Receipt with decision = â€œPassâ€ and freeze all analysis artifacts.

16.1.2 Secondary outcomes (non-claiming)Inconclusive. Some, but not all, items pass (e.g., two lab channels pass but LLR is neutral). We publish full packs and a non-claim ToE receipt with â€œInconclusive; continue acquisitionâ€.Null. No p-hacking: thresholds are fixed.Numerics in receipt. {AÌ‚â‚shâ‚, Ï„Ì‚â‚shâ‚, Ï„Ì‚â‚Aâ‚, vÌ‚â‚frontâ‚, Î³Ì‚, Î¸Ì„} with HPDs; Bayes factors; Î”elpdâ‚looâ‚; guardrail checklist; audit signatures; SHA-256 roots.16.1.5 Contract (takeaway)

17.1 Conceptual implications (push vs. pull; boundary control)
Push, not pull. Causality made operational. Because Ï‡ transport has a finite speed câ‚Ï‡â‚ â‰¤ 1, changes in Î¸â‚Gâ‚(t) propagate with a front vâ‚frontâ‚ â‰¤ câ‚Ï‡â‚. Proof. Â§E.3 gives finite impulse and velocity limits. Â§E.4 yields asymptotically free motion. Â§E.5 gives U(t) â†’ 0. âˆ

E.7 Corollary (N-body dispersion)
Let N â‰¥ 3 bodies evolve under the same assumptions H1â€“H3 (now for N bodies) and with the same non-collision envelope after some Tâ‚€. Then:All velocities vâ‚aâ‚(âˆ) exist and the CM velocity is 0.The configuration decomposes into a (possibly empty) finite collection of scattering clusters, each moving with a cluster CM velocity and with internal relative velocities converging; in every case U(t) â†’ 0 because G(t) â†’ 0 and Uâ‚0â‚ is a sum of 1â„r terms.Any initially bound cluster (negative internal energy) cannot remain bound at late times: EÌ‡(t) â‰¥ 0 and G(t) â†’ 0 together force the effective binding potential to evaporate (internal U â†’ 0), so the cluster either (a) freezes (all internal v â†’ 0, a degenerate free motion) or (b) disperses (some internal v â†’ nonzero). In both (a) and (b), the internal dynamics are asymptotically free.(Sketch.) The proof is the same finite-impulse argument: once pairwise accelerations are bounded by G(t) times an integrable envelope, the velocities converge and trajectories linearize. U(t) = G(t)Â·Uâ‚0â‚(x(t)) â†’ 0 termwise, hence in total. âˆ

E.8 Diagnostics and rates (practical bounds)Velocity convergence rate. For any t â‰¥ T â‰¥ Tâ‚€,
|vâ‚aâ‚(t) âˆ’ vâ‚aâ‚(T)| â‰¤ mâ‚aâ‚â»Â¹ âˆ«â‚Tâ‚â½tâ¾ G(s)Â·Câ‚€Â·(1 + R(s))â½âˆ’2â¾ ds â‰¤ mâ‚aâ‚â»Â¹Â·Câ‚€ âˆ«â‚Tâ‚â½âˆâ¾ G(s) ds.
Thus the Cauchy tail is controlled by the tail integral of G.Position remainder. |râ‚aâ‚(t) âˆ’ (qâ‚aâ‚ + vâ‚aâ‚(âˆ)Â·t)| â‰¤ âˆ«â‚tâ„2â‚â½âˆâ¾ (s âˆ’ tâ„2)Â·|vÌ‡â‚aâ‚(s)| ds = o(1).Virial envelope. JÌˆ(t) = 2E(t) âˆ’ U(t) â‰¥ 2E(0), so J(t) is uniformly convex. This prevents recurrent tight clustering at late times when combined with finite impulse (no sustained negative-U trapping).E.9 Remarks and edge cases
R1 (near-collisions). If a finite number of near-collisions occur after Tâ‚€, each contributes a finite impulse because the time weight G(t) is small late and the Kepler flyby is of finite measure. The same conclusion holds.
R2 (measure-zero singular sets). Classical three-body triple collisions require zero angular momentum and special initial data. Excluding this meagre set gives H2 generically.
R3 (what the theorem does not assert). We do not claim a universal rate U(t) â†’ 0 beyond the trivial G(t) factor, nor do we forbid the â€œfreezeâ€ outcome (vâ‚relâ‚ â†’ 0) within a bounded cluster; both are asymptotically free in the CM sense.

E.10 Contract (takeaway)
With G(t) monotone and integrable, the Ï‡-driven attraction exerts only a finite late-time impulse. That suffices to make velocities converge and trajectories linearize, while U(t) â†’ 0 because G(t) â†’ 0 and the configuration either spreads or freezes. This proves the three-body suppression regime we use in the paper and extends to N bodies under the same mild, generic regularity assumptions.

H. Strong-field Ï‡ on Kerr; BH thermodynamics; GSL details
Goal. Preregistration artifacts: Nexus Ops Card; Ignition Ledger; instrument configs; templates
Aim. Freeze every decision before data-taking: who/what/when/how ignition is declared; how instruments are configured; how lags, anisotropy, and steps are fit; how hashes and nulls are recorded. This appendix supplies drop-in templates you can mint (unchanged) as DOIs.

N.2 Likelihoods and priors

Priors (weakly informative).

N.4 Identification & regularizationShoulder vs OU leakage. Enforce orthogonality by excluding f â‰ª 1â„Ï„â‚shâ‚ from the phase-slope band and using prior shrinkage on Ïƒâ‚Aâ‚.Gainâ€“amplitude confounding. Kalman formulation naturally handles gaps; apply 4Ïƒ clipping on residuals as in configs.N.5 Inference workflow (deterministic)Hash check. Verify SHA-256 of all packs (LEDGER, LAG, ANI, ODF, CFG).Env freeze. Create environment (see N.6) and record pip freeze / conda env export.Preprocess. Apply preregistered filters and resampling; lock RNG seeds (Appendix M).Lag fit. Run spectral + matched-filter pipelines; save Î”tÌ‚, HPDs, cone plots; compute câ‚Ï‡â‚ bound.State-space fit. Compute PSIS-LOO/WAIC; optionally nested sampling to cross-check evidence.Posterior predictive checks. Simulate yÌƒ under posterior; compare PSDs, autocovariances, step-onset histograms.Receipts. Write JSON summaries with medians, HPDs, diagnostics; re-hash outputs; update the Ledger mirror.N.6 Code notes (stack, numerics, seeds)Languages. Reference implementation in Python; mirror notebooks in Juliaâ„R optional.Packages (pin versions). numpy, scipy, numba, matplotlib, xarray; SSM via pykalman or custom JAX; MCMC via numpyroâ„pymc (NUTS), or stan.Linear algebra. Use stabilized Kalman (Joseph form); square-root filters for long Ï„â‚Aâ‚. PSDs computed with multitaper (K â‰¥ 3).Randomness. Single master seed per run; record in Ledger.Tolerance. Cholesky jitter 1eâˆ’9; clip |Ï•| â‰¤ 0.999999 for OU AR(1) equivalents.Performance. Chunk by day; vectorize per site; avoid FFT leakage (tapers + zero-pads).(In code/JSON use ASCII subscripts: e.g., tau_A_s, A_sh.)

O.6 Universality ratios and acceptance windows

Ramanâ€“gap scaling (ğ•Œ). Prediction ğ•Œ â‰ˆ 1â„2 near small |r|; accept if ğ•Œ âˆˆ [0.4, 0.6] across at least three Îµ windows; reject if ğ•Œ consistently outside [0.3, 0.7] with proper error bars.

Topo toggle. If gatingâ„strain crosses Î” minimum, the edge mid-gap STS peak must diminish/vanish when entering the trivial side and reappear when returning (no hysteresis beyond contact drift). Failure to toggle under clean control rejects topological SSH semantics for the device.

O.7 Falsification & foils
Hard falsifiers.

ğ•Œ far from 1â„2 with stable signals and verified strain (rules out the soft-mode scaling).

Î¥ far from 1 after vâ‚Fâ‚ calibration (rules out Î¾ âˆ 1â„Î” edge physics).

No edge state at all in long, clean chains (rules out topology or indicates different terminations/chemistry).

Soft foils to test.

Polyyne vs cumulene mix. Two-phase segments give Raman multi-peaks; treat as composition foil.

Electronâ€“phonon nonlinearity. If Ï‰â‚BOWâ‚ âˆ |r|â½Î½â‚ with Î½ â‰  1â„2, report Î½ with errors; repeated Î½ â‰ˆ 1 implies different mechanism (reject SSH minimality).
